Just taking the time to say that I really appreciated the awesome experience that I had with all the team players at this office starting with the manager Sylvia. She made us feel very welcomed with a beautiful smile and such great customer service skills. She built up rapport which I feel is very important to keeping service levels high. After getting the xray results; she broke down the cost to us completely and outlined all the work to be done for both my son and I. We were able to use our $100.00 coupon towards our first visit; so we didn't have to come out of our pockets for the first service for my son. Which we felt really good about. We're also able to stretch out the appointments so we're not being hit with out of pockets expenses right away. There was no pressure to get it done quickly like some management teams try to do. Makes the experience feel like just a numbers game; but not at Aava Dental, Upland office. Sylvia also manages about 3 other offices and I'm sure she manages then well too.

Now for the assistant Denise to Dr.Parker; she was super friendly and very professional. You could tell that she knew her skills 100%. She explained the process and made you feel very at ease. She also built up rapport which is essential to making a patient feel relaxed. My son Brandon especially appreciated her and was impressed with her skill level as an assistant. We both enjoyed working with her.

Finally for Dr. Parker, she's an awesomely great dentist. She knows her skill well. She's been practicing these skills obviously for a long time. She made us both feel very comfortable with talking with us beforehand and getting to know us. She asked about our family and showed concern for our well being. She didn't try to sell us on expensive procedures; but she did explain the advantages of doing one over the other which I highly appreciated. I give her personally 5 star for making us feel at ease with the overall experience as a great dentist.

Aava Dental can consider us lifetime patients. We will be referring other family members here if they're in need of a new dental office. My mom already said that she's in and she'll be visiting the office soon. I don't mind sending people to where I know their experience will be rewarding. Thanks ladies for your outstanding service!!!!!< /Review>

< Review>
Located off Carson in Torrance. Small parking lot shared with other businesses during the day time parking will probably be tight after the other businesses close parking would be better. The place is small they have a big table in the middle to accommodate a big party and a couple of booths along the side and a few rooms to sit Japanese style where you take your shoes off. The staff was friendly and service was pretty fast. I wasn't hungry for ramen so I just got some edamame. Our server was very attentive and apologized for either missing something or taking long for anything I think he was overwhelmed with the big table party but he was cool and took care of us. Overall a nice spot for a late ramen craving. I'd go back for ramen.</Review>

<rating>3<//rating>< text>
Great customer service. The wait staff really knew their menu. I read the other reviews and couldn't disagree more with the bad service. Zabon's has a hip young multi racial staff which I found to be a refreshing  change of pace from the usual ramen shops in the South Bay Los Angeles area. Beautiful simple traditional Japanese decor. Spotlessly clean. I ordered the spicy ramen from their lunch menu. Only 8.95$. 2.00-3.00$ less than a bowl of ramen in the same area. The broth was a bit on the salty side for me. Portion size and soup temperature on point. Fast service.<//text>

<review>This is your typical Japanese ramen shop: a few tables, a mini bar, and a few booths.

There is a large room on the left upon entering, and is normally occupied. I can say the same towards the booths (towards the right, window view of Carson St) but not as frequent compared to the former.

Service is fantastic, the servers check on you from time to time, unlike other places where they just seat you and, well, good luck getting service!

I get the usual [will update this later of the specific order when I visit again as well as include a picture of the menu(s) for your convenience].

If you're not familiar with Japanese cuisine, the portions are VERY SMALL compared to American cuisine, so don't be surprised if you order anything that ISN'T ramen and find that it looks rather skimpy.

I don't know if they have a customer-usable restroom as I never asked (will add on next visit).

I always come back for the spontaneous ramen cravings!!!<//review>< pictures>

<review>Came here because my cousin said it was good so I just had to try it out. Its a fair sized place with i believe 2 enclosed tables, we sat in one of them. It's both a pro and con because yes its enclosed but it made it easy to forget we were there. Also being busy made it easy to forget us since our table wasn't in eye sight. Service could have been a tad better but it was still good. My waitress stayed helpful and positive which is always great. Now as far as food goes I had the takoyaki and small curry rice to start, both of which were great delicious starters. My main course was their spicy miso ramen but I had to add flavored egg and seaweed since I love having both in all my ramen. Be aware that the spicy miso ramen doesn't come with egg already. Almost every other ramen spot I have been to has it already included in the ramen so that was different. The seaweed however wasn't how I prefer seaweed on my ramen. This place had it chopped up and it was moist served on the side. Other spots serve it dried and in 1 or 2 large pieces inside the ramen; that's how I prefer it. Overall the ramen was great and filling. I wish I could try it with sake and dessert but I'll save that for next time. I do recommend this place and I will return for another time.</review>< Rate>

<Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipORzl-g090ckdENBojo6J9z935TzhhH2rnvJNXq=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNYQWcUXteRakw5cYPsrTnSLm2CnSwRPDqBuFeF=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>< Text>
Swank farm creates one of the largest corn stalk mazes in the country each October. More than a mile square, intrepid adventurers enter the maze with a map and try and locate about 25-30 spots where they find words that complete the annual story. It is all good.m clean fun. Low wattage/ dim flashlights are a must.

The farm also features two bouncy pillows ( one for younger kids and one for older kids), peddle cart racing track, goat petting zoo, giant pumpkin slings and corn husk air cannons- all for one entry price. In addition, there is a scary-ish haunted house for older kids, a pumpkin patch, as well as home made fudge available for purchase.

Perfect for kids of all ages.

Note: it can get chilly at night so best to be prepared. Bring water bottles, flashlights and  closed shoes. If rain is forecast, know that the parking lot is dirt and will quickly turn muddy.<//Text>

< Review>
This place was the first haunted house experience I have ever had in my life and it got me hooked and that was 15 years ago.

This place has never disappoint me each time I go I really look forward to solving the fill in the blank with the maze.

Each year there is a new theme for the haunted house so you don't have to be afraid of experiencing the same thing as last year.

There are other things to do besides the haunted house such as the pedal karts, petting zoo, this year didn't have the pig. They have a pumpkin patch they have a kitty Zone this year they have added a train.

Your ticket price includes everything inside so you can go to the jumpy house as much as you want you can pedal cart as much as you want you can jump on the big pillow as much as you want.

It takes about one hour and a half to drive from Oakland to Hollister but I think it's worth it<//Review>

It was barren, alot of walking space with no one popping out, alot of empty crevices and hiding spaces youd assume actors would come out of but they were empty. I get scared easily too but this was horrible. I wish I could get my money back. Especially the food stands. We wanted nachos they said its a 30min wait because their making a fresh batch, so we said ok, tacos then. They said its a 45 min wait because their cooking that too. So we just got churros and watered down hot chocolate. We went to another fudge store and ordered hot dogs and they had NO drinks inside the fridge except a few diet Pepsi and water. We had to wait 20min for them to get their delivery of soda to restock. The entire experience sucked. Tomorrow is my birthday so this weekend was supposed to be my birthday weekend of fun and it was ultimately a waste of my time, travel (I came from San jose) and a good $100. (39 per ticket so $78) for my fiance and I. Wish we could get our money back, entire way home I was pissed.<//text>

<rate>4< /rate><Review>My family and I came across Tajima Ramen when we were in Long Beach a couple years ago. There's something about the name I find comforting - a sense of familiarity. Anyway, we thought it was good and that was that.

Fast forward a couple years and my daughter and I were in San Diego. After the obligatory stop at the San Diego Zoo (we were visiting from Vegas), we were hungry and looking for a place to grab lunch before our kayaking trip in La Jolla (see my review). And wouldn't you know it - there was a Tajima Ramen ten minutes away.

There were only two other parties there when we got there so we were seated right away. The place is clean and the servers were both friendly. We ordered the Tajima Ramen and the Salmon Poke Bowl. The ramen noodles were good, the flavor of the soup was good, and the unsliced chashu slab was something I'd never seen before.

This is personal preference but I prefer the soup to be piping hot. The soup definitely wasn't hot - like if it spilled it on me, I wouldn't get a burn - and maybe that's why they do it intentionally. Or are there food safety regulations put in place by the heath department that don't allow items to be served above a certain temperature?

Whatever the reason, this made me sad. The Salmon Poke Bowl looked great and had all the toppings to make it a hit- but I thought the salmon could've been a little bit fresher. Maybe they don't sell a bunch of these so inventory sits for a while?

All in all, a solid place for lunch!< /Review>< pics>

<rate>5</rate><Text>It was a slightly rainy and dreary day and so when my super special man friend suggested we go for Ramen I was sold.
He is a San Diego local and I am a mere visitor so when he took me to Tajima I had no idea what I was getting into.
There was a short wait but we were seated outside promptly under the heaters with the perfect temperature. We started with the tempura brussels and the umami pork bun. Somehow my friend had only ordered one bun. Are you kidding me? I could eat 5 of those myself. They were that good!
He did redeem himself however when we ordered the ramen, going with the Classic Tajima Ramen and the Spicy Sesame Ramen.
FLA-VA! So Much FLA-VA. Both were amazing and I may have even let him have a bite or two, but not much more.
Now can we talk about Nick, our server. Fan Freakin Tastic. He had all the answers, was super accommodating (since someone at the table is one of those high maintenance people who thinks that they are low maintenance. :)), and was just on top of everything from start to finish.
He made our night!
This out-of-towner was duly impressed.

<date>1562306045234< /date>< text>
My family and I came across Tajima Ramen when we were in Long Beach a couple years ago. There's something about the name I find comforting - a sense of familiarity. Anyway, we thought it was good and that was that.

Fast forward a couple years and my daughter and I were in San Diego. After the obligatory stop at the San Diego Zoo (we were visiting from Vegas), we were hungry and looking for a place to grab lunch before our kayaking trip in La Jolla (see my review). And wouldn't you know it - there was a Tajima Ramen ten minutes away.

There were only two other parties there when we got there so we were seated right away. The place is clean and the servers were both friendly. We ordered the Tajima Ramen and the Salmon Poke Bowl. The ramen noodles were good, the flavor of the soup was good, and the unsliced chashu slab was something I'd never seen before.

This is personal preference but I prefer the soup to be piping hot. The soup definitely wasn't hot - like if it spilled it on me, I wouldn't get a burn - and maybe that's why they do it intentionally. Or are there food safety regulations put in place by the heath department that don't allow items to be served above a certain temperature?

Whatever the reason, this made me sad. The Salmon Poke Bowl looked great and had all the toppings to make it a hit- but I thought the salmon could've been a little bit fresher. Maybe they don't sell a bunch of these so inventory sits for a while?

All in all, a solid place for lunch!</text>

Decent Ramen bar. Prices around $11/bowl. Parking can be difficult to find as street parking or the Rite Aid pay parking lot are your only choices. < text>
Yea why not a four star, I ask myself as I determine what it should be.  Although I don't think Tajima is as good as Santouka, they are good enough for me to keep coming again and again.  So because of this I'm definitely a fan.

Ordered their edamame and just don't do it, not worth it. Very salty for some reason. Stick with the ramen only. I usually order the Tonkatsu Ramen that has everything in it. I like the taste and the fact that the broth doesn't taste too fatty.

Great place to go to if you're close by. The service has been great the both times I have been there even at their busiest. Don't forget to write your name on the stand when they are busy. They do go off that list.

Enjoy!< /text>

<review>First time checking out this place on a Saturday evening. Thought it would be super packed, but nope,  not at all. Got seated right away & mentioned to the waiter it was our first time trying out ramen. He got all excited and happy that we chose Tajima. He explained the menu and I ordered the Vegan Ramen with spinach noodles. Waited about 10 mins or so for the ramen. I love soups and being able to try ramen for the first time was exciting!

So, our order comes out and the bowl is a very decent size bowl. Im thinking I might not be able to finish it all. The ramen bowl had all sorts of veggies, mushrooms, corn, tofu, asparagus and mixed green lettuce. The broth is creamy and smelled delish! Overall the taste of the was good, but it was a bit too salty for me. Not sure if ramen is suppose to be on the salty side, but I had like 4 glasses of water and I hadn't even finished. I would have liked more corn and mushrooms - (not sure whats up with the mixed green lettuce, maybe next time I'll order it with no lettuce)

I will give this place another try once colder weather hits.

3/5 stars due to the saltiness.<//review>< pictures>
None< /pictures>

<userid>100366113117526980111< /userid>< user_name>
Jen H< /user_name>
<Date>1423199075031</Date><rating>5</rating>< Text>
SO VERY GOOD.

Probably one of the best ramens I've had thus far.

Their broth had so much flavor without it being super super greasy (something I look for is if the broth sort of congeals as the temperature cools, and theirs didn't!) Their noodles were perfect and they had different options to accommodate your noodle preference. AND THE PORK.. oh the pork... it was fantastic. They give nice, thick, fat cuts of pork. My bowl of ramen was just perfection. I also want to point out that the seaweed was super tasty, and normally i don't really care for seaweed. I highly recommend getting the tajima ramen with thick noodles and make it spicy!

I also tried their takoyaki and gyoza and they were both delicious. If you want a drink to go with your meal, try the wasabi beer if they have it! The beer has a unique taste at the end, it doesn't really taste like wasabi but it was good. I don't think you can find it in a lot of places so it's worth getting here to enjoy with your meal :)

It's usually pretty crowded, so the wait time is long especially for larger parties greater than 4. They have one large communal table and a couple of tables for 2 or 4 people. Parking is only available on the street.

DEFINITELY A MUST TRY IF YOU'RE A RAMEN FAN.<//Text>

<Review>Absolutely insane food. Despite it being a bit late and a bit crowded, me and my partner quickly got seated, thought food did take a bit (no big deal though). We ordered the tajima ramen, and let me say it is one of the best ramen I think I have ever had. The earthy root vegetables paired well with the pork, the broth base was a very rich flavor that was cut by the green onions, but paired well with the noodles and the slightly sweet egg. I could honestly go on and on, a masterclass in building ramen.

I will say though, despite it being incredibly good, dont confuse it for authentic, I have tried "authentic" ramen before and it wasn't anywhere near the flavor of this. I felt it was very americanized, especially the broth, which tasted more "chicken soup" than anything. Is this a bad thing? No, not at all, considering it is up there with the best ramen ive ever had.

One of the few food places in San Diego that made me sit down and actually think about well made the dish was in the middle of the meal. Absolutely do yourself a favor and come here and get the tajima ramen, you wont regret it.< /Review>< GmapID>
